class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>legislatures and legislation of the United Kingdom</b> derive from a number of different sources from both within the UK and through membership of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> is the supreme <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative body</a> for the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territories" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territories">British overseas territories</a> with Scotland, Wales and Northern Ireland each having their own devolved legislatures. Each of the three major <a href="/wiki/Jurisdiction_(area)" title="Jurisdiction (area)">jurisdictions</a> of the United Kingdom (<a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>) has its own <a href="/wiki/Laws" class="mw-redirect" title="Laws">laws</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legal_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal system">legal system</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span id="United_Kingdom_legislature_.26_English_law"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom_legislature_&amp;_English_law">United Kingdom legislature &amp; English law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: United Kingdom legislature &amp; English law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Northern_Ireland">The Parliament of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The Parliament of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palace_of_Westminster_-_Clock_Tower_and_New_Palace_Yard_from_the_west_-_240404.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Sand-coloured building of Gothic design with large clock-tower." href="/wiki/File:Palace_of_Westminster_-_Clock_Tower_and_New_Palace_Yard_from_the_west_-_240404.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The UK Parliament meets at the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg" class="image"><img alt="United Kingdom in the British Isles.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg/120px-United_Kingdom_in_the_British_Isles.svg.png" width="120" height="210" /></a></div>\n<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_England_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of England within the United Kingdom.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Map_of_England_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/120px-Map_of_England_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="120" height="186" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Map_of_England_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/180px-Map_of_England_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, /></a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">Government of the United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_England" title="Local government in England">Local government in England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Parliament_(UK)" title="Act of Parliament (UK)">Act of Parliament (UK)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statutory_instrument_(UK)" title="Statutory instrument (UK)">Statutory instrument (UK)</a>, <a href="/wiki/UK_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Law">UK Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="English Law">English Law</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Reserved_and_excepted_matters" title="Reserved and excepted matters">Reserved and excepted matters</a></div>\n<p>The United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland (commonly known as the UK Parliament, the British Parliament, the Westminster Parliament or "Westminster") is the supreme legislative body for the United Kingdom and also for English Law. It alone possesses <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_sovereignty" title="Parliamentary sovereignty">legislative supremacy</a> and thereby ultimate power over all other political bodies in the UK and its territories. Its head is the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Monarchy of the United Kingdom">Sovereign of the United Kingdom</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth II</a>) and its seat is the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a> in <a href="/wiki/Westminster" title="Westminster">Westminster</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.\n</p><p>The United Kingdom Legislation may take the form of <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Parliament_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Acts of Parliament in the United Kingdom">Acts</a> (passed directly by Parliament) or <a href="/wiki/Statutory_Instrument" class="mw-redirect" title="Statutory Instrument">Statutory Instruments</a>, made under the authority of an Act of Parliament by either a <a href="/wiki/Minister_(government)" title="Minister (government)">government minister</a> or by the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Privy Council of the United Kingdom">Queen-in-Council</a>. The latter are generally subject either to parliamentary approval (affirmative procedure) or parliamentary disallowance (negative procedure). The majority of Acts considered in the UK are defined as public general acts, or \'Acts of Parliament\' as they will have progressed and gained approval as a Bill through both House of Commons and House of Lords, and also have gained Royal Assent from the Monarch. <a href="/wiki/Local_and_personal_Acts_of_Parliament_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Local and personal Acts of Parliament in the United Kingdom">Local and Personal Acts of Parliament</a> are also presented to Parliament as a result of sponsored petitions. These, however, are processed through committees to enable relevant or affected parties to challenge or change the proposed Act.   <a href="/wiki/Prerogative_instrument" title="Prerogative instrument">Prerogative instruments</a>, made by the Sovereign under the <a href="/wiki/Royal_prerogative" title="Royal prerogative">royal prerogative</a> are another source of UK-wide legislation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. The UK Parliament is responsible for all matters relating to defence and all foreign affairs and relations with international organisations,  particularly the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.\n</p><p>With there being no devolved legislature in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> the UK Parliament is also the supreme body for its governance, legislation, public bodies and local government.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Commons">House of Commons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: House of Commons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<p>The House of Commons is the lower house of the Parliament of the United Kingdom and is an elected chamber consisting currently of 650 members known as <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament_(United_Kingdom)" title="Member of Parliament (United Kingdom)">Members of Parliament</a> (MPs) which are elected using <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">First past the post</a> in single-member <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Parliamentary_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Parliamentary constituencies">constituencies</a> with 533 elected from <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, 59 from <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, 40 from <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> and 18 from <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. \n</p><p>The House of Commons is now considered to be the supreme chamber of Parliament.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Lords">House of Lords</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: House of Lords">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Lords of the United Kingdom">House of Lords of the United Kingdom</a></div>\n<p>The House of Lords is the upper house of the Parliament of the United Kingdom however it is an unelected chamber with all members to the House of Lords being appointed. As of August 2018, there are currently 793 members known as "Peers". The House of Lords no longer has the same powers as the House of Commons under the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Acts" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament Acts">Parliament Acts of 1911 and 1949</a> especially when it comes to blocking general legislation and the passing of financial legislation.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Devolved_legisatures_and_law">Devolved legisatures and law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Devolved legisatures and law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Devolution_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Devolution in the United Kingdom">Devolution in the United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joint_Ministerial_Committee_(UK)" title="Joint Ministerial Committee (UK)">Joint Ministerial Committee (UK)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Consent_Motion" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative Consent Motion">Legislative Consent Motion</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Scottish_Parliament">The Scottish Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Scottish Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Edinburgh_Scottish_Parliament01_2006-04-29_crop1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Edinburgh_Scottish_Parliament01_2006-04-29_crop1.jpg/160px-Edinburgh_Scottish_Parliament01_2006-04-29_crop1.jpg" width="160" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Edinburgh_Scottish_Parliament01_2006-04-29_crop1.jpg/240px-Edinburgh_Scottish_Parliament01_2006-04-29_crop1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Edinburgh_Scottish_Parliament01_2006-04-29_crop1.jpg/320px-Edinburgh_Scottish_Parliament01_2006-04-29_crop1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1642" data-file-height="1044" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Edinburgh_Scottish_Parliament01_2006-04-29_crop1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Scottish Parliament meets at <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament_Building" title="Scottish Parliament Building">Holyrood</a> in <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>.</div></div></div>    \n<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Scotland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of Scotland within the United Kingdom.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Map_of_Scotland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/120px-Map_of_Scotland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="120" height="186" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Map_of_Scotland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/180px-Map_of_Scotland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Map_of_Scotland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/240px-Map_of_Scotland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="616" data-file-height="955" /></a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Scotland" title="Local government in Scotland">Local government in Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Act of the Scottish Parliament">Act of the Scottish Parliament</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_statutory_instrument" title="Scottish statutory instrument">Scottish statutory instrument</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scots_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots Law">Scots Law</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Parliament" title="Scottish Parliament">Scottish Parliament</a> is the national, <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> legislature of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Holyrood,_Edinburgh" title="Holyrood, Edinburgh">Holyrood</a> area of the capital, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>. The Parliament, informally referred to as "Holyrood",<sup id="cite_ref-HolyroodName_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HolyroodName-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> is a democratically elected body comprising 129 members known as <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Scottish_Parliament" title="Member of the Scottish Parliament">Members of the Scottish Parliament</a> (MSPs). Of these 73 MSPs are elected using <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">First past the post</a> in single member constituencies and a further 56 MSPs are elected using the <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D&#39;Hondt method">D\'Hondt method</a>, a form of party-list proportional representation in eight additional member regions with each region electing 7 MSPs.\n</p><p>The Scottish Parliament was convened by the <a href="/wiki/Scotland_Act_1998" title="Scotland Act 1998">Scotland Act 1998</a>, which sets out its powers as a <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved</a> legislature. The Act delineates the legislative competence of the Parliament&#160;&#8211;&#32;the areas in which it can make <a href="/wiki/Scots_law" title="Scots law">laws</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32;by explicitly specifying powers that are "<a href="/wiki/Reserved_matters" class="mw-redirect" title="Reserved matters">reserved</a>" to the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament of the United Kingdom</a>: all matters that are not explicitly reserved are automatically the responsibility of the Scottish Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-SpecifiedReservations_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpecifiedReservations-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The British Parliament retains the ability to amend the terms of reference of the Scottish Parliament, and can extend or reduce the areas in which it can make laws.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The first meeting of the new Parliament took place on 12 May 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-FirstMeeting_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FirstMeeting-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Statutory_Instrument" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Statutory Instrument">Scottish Statutory Instruments</a> made by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Government" title="Scottish Government">Scottish Government</a> are another source of legislation. As with Statutory Instruments made by the British government, these are generally subject to either approval or disallowance by the Scottish Parliament\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_National_Assembly_for_Wales">The National Assembly for Wales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The National Assembly for Wales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Senedd,_Welsh_parliament,_Cardiff_Bay.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Senedd%2C_Welsh_parliament%2C_Cardiff_Bay.jpg/160px-Senedd%2C_Welsh_parliament%2C_Cardiff_Bay.jpg" width="160" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Senedd%2C_Welsh_parliament%2C_Cardiff_Bay.jpg/240px-Senedd%2C_Welsh_parliament%2C_Cardiff_Bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Senedd%2C_Welsh_parliament%2C_Cardiff_Bay.jpg/320px-Senedd%2C_Welsh_parliament%2C_Cardiff_Bay.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4886" data-file-height="3054" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Senedd,_Welsh_parliament,_Cardiff_Bay.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Welsh Assembly meets in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a></div></div></div>    \n<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Wales_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of Wales within the United Kingdom.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_of_Wales_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/120px-Map_of_Wales_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="120" height="186" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_of_Wales_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/180px-Map_of_Wales_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Map_of_Wales_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/240px-Map_of_Wales_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="616" data-file-height="955" /></a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="National Assembly for Wales">National Assembly for Wales</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Wales" title="First Minister of Wales">First Minister of Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Government" title="Welsh Government">Welsh Government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Wales" title="Local government in Wales">Local government in Wales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="Act of the National Assembly for Wales">Act of the National Assembly for Wales</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Law">Welsh Law</a></div>\n<p>The National Assembly for Wales has the power to make legislation in Wales. The Assembly was created by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Wales_Act_1998" title="Government of Wales Act 1998">Government of Wales Act 1998</a>, which followed a <a href="/wiki/Wales_referendum_1997" class="mw-redirect" title="Wales referendum 1997">referendum</a> in 1997. It is a  democratically elected body with 60 members known as <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="Member of the National Assembly for Wales">Assembly Members</a> (AMs). Of these 40 AMs are elected using <a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">First past the post</a> in single member constituencies and a further 20 MSPs are elected using the <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D&#39;Hondt method">D\'Hondt method</a>, a form of party-list proportional representation in five additional member regions with each region electing 4 AMs. The Assembly had no powers to initiate <a href="/wiki/Primary_legislation" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary legislation">primary legislation</a> until limited law-making powers were gained through the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Wales_Act_2006" title="Government of Wales Act 2006">Government of Wales Act 2006</a>. Its primary law-making powers were enhanced following a Yes vote in the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_devolution_referendum,_2011" title="Welsh devolution referendum, 2011">referendum</a> on 3 March 2011, making it possible for it to <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_National_Assembly_for_Wales" title="Act of the National Assembly for Wales">legislate</a> in the 20 areas that are devolved without having to consult the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">UK Parliament</a>, nor the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Wales" title="Secretary of State for Wales">Secretary of State for Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The Assembly may also delegate authority to enact legislation through Welsh Statutory Instruments. Under the <a href="/wiki/Wales_Act_2017" title="Wales Act 2017">Wales Act 2017</a> the Assembly came into line with Scotland and Northern Ireland and moved to a resevered powers model. \n</p><p>It is expected that the National Assembly for Wales will be renamed the "Welsh Parliament" before the next scheduled election in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Northern_Ireland_Assembly">The Northern Ireland Assembly</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The Northern Ireland Assembly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stormont_Parliamentary_Building_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Stormont_Parliamentary_Building_01.JPG/160px-Stormont_Parliamentary_Building_01.JPG" width="160" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Stormont_Parliamentary_Building_01.JPG/240px-Stormont_Parliamentary_Building_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Stormont_Parliamentary_Building_01.JPG/320px-Stormont_Parliamentary_Building_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1701" data-file-height="1199" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stormont_Parliamentary_Building_01.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Northern Ireland Assembly meets at <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Buildings_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Parliament Buildings (Northern Ireland)">Stormont</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Northern_Ireland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of Northern Ireland within the United Kingdom.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_of_Northern_Ireland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/120px-Map_of_Northern_Ireland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="120" height="186" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_of_Northern_Ireland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/180px-Map_of_Northern_Ireland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Map_of_Northern_Ireland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg/240px-Map_of_Northern_Ireland_within_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="616" data-file-height="955" /></a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Assembly" title="Northern Ireland Assembly">Northern Ireland Assembly</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_and_deputy_First_Minister_of_Northern_Ireland" title="First Minister and deputy First Minister of Northern Ireland">First Minister and deputy First Minister of Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Executive" title="Northern Ireland Executive">Northern Ireland Executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_Northern_Ireland" title="Local government in Northern Ireland">Local government in Northern Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Act_of_the_Northern_Ireland_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly">Act of the Northern Ireland Assembly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Law">Northern Ireland Law</a></div>\n<p>The Northern Ireland Assembly is the <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved</a> legislature of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> which is a democratically elected body comprising 90 members known as <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Legislative_Assembly_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Member of the Legislative Assembly (Northern Ireland)">Members of the Legislative Assembly</a> (MLAs). The 90 MLAs are elected using the <a href="/wiki/Single_transferable_vote" title="Single transferable vote">single transferable vote</a> across the 18 <a href="/wiki/List_of_parliamentary_constituencies_in_Northern_Ireland" title="List of parliamentary constituencies in Northern Ireland">Westminster Parliamentary constituencies</a> with each constituency electing 5 MLAs. It was established in 1998 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement" title="Good Friday Agreement">Good Friday Agreement</a> which was approved by the public in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Good_Friday_Agreement_referendum,_1998" title="Northern Ireland Good Friday Agreement referendum, 1998">referendums which were held in both Northern Ireland and in the Republic of Ireland</a>. It has power to legislate in a wide range of areas that are not explicitly <a href="/wiki/Reserved_matters" class="mw-redirect" title="Reserved matters">reserved</a> to the Parliament of the United Kingdom, and to appoint the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Executive" title="Northern Ireland Executive">Northern Ireland Executive</a>. It sits at <a href="/wiki/Parliament_Buildings_(Northern_Ireland)" title="Parliament Buildings (Northern Ireland)">Parliament Buildings</a> at <a href="/wiki/Stormont,_Belfast" class="mw-redirect" title="Stormont, Belfast">Stormont</a> in <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">Belfast</a>.  Legislation of the Assembly empowers the Northern Island Executive to issue <a href="/wiki/Statutory_Rules_of_Northern_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Statutory Rules of Northern Ireland">Statutory Rules</a> in a variety of areas.\n</p><p>The Assembly currently hasn\xe2\x80\x99t met since 26 January 2017 due to a breakdown of trust which brought down both the Assembly and Executive.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="European_Union_legislature_.26_law"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union_legislature_&amp;_law">European Union legislature &amp; law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: European Union legislature &amp; law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="vertical-navbox vcard" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Europe.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Europe.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/32px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" width="32" title="Portal:European Union">European Union&#32;portal</a> <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Template talk:Politics of the European Union"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decision_(European_Union_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Decision (European Union law)">Decision (European Union law)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Directive_(European_Union_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Directive (European Union law)">Directive (European Union law)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Regulation_(European_Union_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Regulation (European Union law)">Regulation (European Union law)</a></div>\n<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) under the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities_Act_1972_(UK)" title="European Communities Act 1972 (UK)">European Communities Act 1972</a> the decisions, directives and regulations of the EU are directly applicable with full legal force in the United Kingdom and is also supreme to all domestic legislation, in effect another source of UK legislation. The United Kingdom became a member when it joined what was originally known as the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a> on 1 January 1973.\n</p><p>Currently the United Kingdom is <a href="/wiki/Brexit_negotiations" title="Brexit negotiations">negotiating</a> its <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">exit</a> from the  organisation and its institutions following a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">referendum in 2016</a> which result in a narrow majority vote in favour of leaving and is expected to officially leave on 30 March 2019. \n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_European_Parliament">The European Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: The European Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a></div>\n<p>The European Parliament (EP) is the <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">directly elected</a> parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">institution of the European Union</a>. Together with the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> (the Council) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, it exercises the legislative function of the EU. The Parliament is composed of 751 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a> (MEPs), who represent the second-largest democratic electorate in the world (after the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_India" title="Parliament of India">Parliament of India</a>) and the largest trans-national democratic electorate in the world (375&#160;million eligible <a href="/wiki/Voting" title="Voting">voters</a> in 2009).<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The United Kingdom sends 73 members to the European Parliament, of these 70 MEPs are elected using the <a href="/wiki/D%27Hondt_method" title="D&#39;Hondt method">D\'Hondt method</a>, a form of party-list proportional representation in 11 regional constituencies in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> while in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> 3 MEPs are elected using the <a href="/wiki/Single_transferable_vote" title="Single transferable vote">single transferable vote</a> in a single national constituency.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_historical_legislatures">The historical legislatures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Legislatures_and_legislation_of_the_United_Kingdom&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The historical legislatures">edit</a><span href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Scotland" title="Parliament of Scotland">Parliament of Scotland</a> (13th century to 1707)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Ireland" title="Parliament of Ireland">Parliament of Ireland</a> (13th century to 1800)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Great_Britain" title="Parliament of Great Britain">Parliament of Great Britain</a> (1707&#8211;1800)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Parliament of Northern Ireland">Parliament of Northern Ireland</a> (1921&#8211;1972)</li></ul>\n<h2><span title="Commonwealth Parliamentary Association">Commonwealth Parliamentary Association</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2"><div><sup><small>1</small></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">European Union law</a> applies in the United Kingdom and <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_invocation_of_Article_50_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union" title="United Kingdom invocation of Article 50 of the Treaty on European Union">invokation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_from_the_European_Union" title="Withdrawal from the European Union">Article 50</a>, the United Kingdom is <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">set to leave</a> the European Union. A <a href="/wiki/European_Union_(Withdrawal)_Act_2018" title="European Union (Withdrawal) Act 2018">Great Repeal Bill</a> has been proposed to incorporate all <i>current</i> European laws into <a href="/wiki/Law_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Law of the United Kingdom">British law</a>.\n<br /><sup><small>2</small></sup> "Bailiwick-wide" legislature passed in the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Guernsey" title="States of Guernsey">States of Guernsey</a> applies not only in <a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, but also in <a href="/wiki/Alderney" title="Alderney">Alderney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sark" title="Sark">Sark</a>, with the consent of their governments.</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<div role="navigation" class="navbox"
